# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Java Annotation Processing for Kafka Config Keys

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that use the @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef annotation pattern for configuration documentation: the annotation definitions, the config documentation generator, and the AbstractConfig subclasses that use annotated config keys.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

management pattern based on the ConfigDef and ConfigKey classes for documenting and managing configuration parameters. This is not based on Java annotations as the task description suggests, but rather on a pattern of class-based configuration definitions.\\n\\n## Core Architecture\\n\\n**ConfigDef (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java)**: The primary class for specifying expected configurations. It contains a nested static class ConfigKey that represents individual configuration parameters. ConfigDef provides methods to define configurations with names, types, default values, documentation, validation logic, groups, ordering, and display information.\\n\\n**ConfigKey (nested in ConfigDef.java)**: A static inner class that encapsulates all metadata for a single configuration key, including: name, type (STRING, INT, LONG, DOUBLE, BOOLEAN, LIST, CLASS, PASSWORD), documentation, defaultValue, validator, importance (HIGH, MEDIUM, LOW), group, orderInGroup, width, displayName, dependents, recommender, internalConfig flag, and alternativeString.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java)**: A base class that provides convenient methods for accessing configuration values. It holds a ConfigDef definition instance and provides methods like typeOf() and documentationOf() that retrieve metadata about configuration keys from the embedded ConfigDef.\\n\\n## Configuration Classes\\n\\nThe pattern is extensively used throughout Kafka across multiple modules:\\n\\n**Client Module**: AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig provide configuration for admin, consumer, and producer clients respectively.\\n\\n**Connect Module**: TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, ConnectorConfig, SourceConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, DistributedConfig, RestServerConfig, ConverterConfig define configurations for Kafka Connect components.\\n\\n**Mirror Module**: MirrorClientConfig, MirrorMakerConfig, MirrorConnectorConfig, MirrorCheckpointConfig, MirrorSourceConfig manage Mirror Maker configurations.\\n\\n**Streams Module**: StreamsConfig and AssignmentConfigs configure Kafka Streams applications.\\n\\n**Server Module**: ServerConfigs, AbstractKafkaConfig, ClientMetricsConfigs define broker-level configurations.\\n\\n**Other Modules**: GroupConfig manages consumer group configurations, LogConfig manages log-level configurations.\\n\\n## Utility and REST Support\\n\\nConfigUtils provides utility methods for working with ConfigDef instances. ConfigKeyInfo (in connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/) provides a REST-friendly representation of ConfigKey metadata. KafkaConfigSchema manages the complete configuration schema for the Kafka broker.\\n\\nThe pattern demonstrates a comprehensive configuration management system where each configuration parameter is formally documented with type information, validation rules, importance levels, and cross-references, enabling both programmatic configuration validation and automated documentation generation.\"\n}\n",

KafkaConfigSchema manages the complete configuration schema for the Kafka broker.\\n\\nThe pattern demonstrates a comprehensive configuration management system where each configuration parameter is formally documented with type information, validation rules, importance levels, and cross-references, enabling both programmatic configuration validation and automated documentation generation.\"\n}\n",
